```
I have been in the World Trade Center thousands of times. The Subway
from New Jersey has (had) its terminal underneath the towers.
  
Today, I figured I could return to business, but found I could not
call into New York City, because all the lines were busy. Then I
noticed that 2 of the people on my call list had addresses in the
World Trade Center...

Yesterday, I was reading my e-mail, when a friend on Instant Messenger
told me that the Twin Towers had collapsed, and the Pentagon and
Pittsburgh had been attacked. I typed out that this was a classic-type
hoax, but checked the news first... Saddest erasure in my life.

My son, John-Paul, lives in Manhattan, but teaches in Brooklyn. The
subway he takes to work runs right near the World Trade Center.  I
called him, left a message on his machine.  Thank God, he had spent
the night in Brooklyn!

Yesterday was a lot like the day Kennedy was killed. Everything
stopped. I was in college, we wandered around, wondering what would
happen.

I've seen too much history. I remember Hiroshima, Kennedy, I met
Malcolm X once, just before he was assassinated, I remember Martin
Luther King, Kent State, now it's ganging up on me, coming faster and
faster, Waco, Ruby Ridge, Murrah Office Building, Columbine, Taliban,
Crazy September.

Please, Lord, make it stop. I'm running out of tears.
```

This was written by Leonard Pitts Jr. in the Miami Herald.

   It's my job to have something to say.  They pay me to provide words
that help make sense of that which troubles the American soul.  But in
this moment of airless shock when hot tears sting disbelieving eyes, the
only thing I can find to say, the only words that seem to fit, must be
addressed to the unknown author of this suffering.

   You monster.  You beast.  You unspeakable bastard.

   What lesson did you hope to teach us by your coward's attack on our
World Trade Center, our Pentagon, us?  What was it you hoped we
would learn? Whatever it was, please know that you failed.

   Did you want us to respect your cause?  You just damned your cause.
   Did you want to make us fear?  You just steeled our resolve.
   Did you want to tear us apart?  You just brought us together.

   Let me tell you about my people.  We are a vast and quarrelsome
family, a family rent by racial, social, political and class division, but a
family nonetheless.  We're frivolous, yes, capable of expending
tremendous emotional energy on pop cultural minutiae--a singer's
revealing dress, a ball team's misfortune, a cartoon mouse.  We're
wealthy, too, spoiled by the ready availability of trinkets and material
goods, and maybe because of that, we walk through life with a certain
sense of blithe entitlement.  We're fundamentally decent, though --
peaceloving and compassionate.  We struggle to know the right thing
and to do it.  And we are, the overwhelming majority of us, people
of faith, believers in a just and loving God.

   Some people -- you, perhaps -- think that any or all of this makes us
weak.  You're mistaken.  We are not weak.  Indeed, we are strong in
ways that cannot be measured by arsenals.

IN PAIN

   Yes, we're in pain now.  We are in mourning and we are in shock.
We're still grappling with the unreality of the awful thing you did, still
working to make ourselves understand that this isn't a special effect
from some Hollywood blockbuster, isn't the plot development from
a Tom Clancy novel.  Both in terms of the awful scope of their
ambition and the probable final death toll, your attacks are likely to go
down as the worst acts of terrorism in the history of the United States
and probably, the history of the world.  You've bloodied us as we
have never been bloodied before.

   But there's a gulf of difference between making us bloody and
making us fall.  This is the lesson Japan was taught to its bitter sorrow
the
last time anyone hit us this hard, the last time anyone brought us such
abrupt and monumental pain.  When roused, we are righteous in our
outrage, terrible in our force.  When provoked by this level of barbarism,
we will bear any suffering, pay any cost, go to any length, in the pursuit
of justice.

   I tell you this without fear of contradiction.  I know my people, as
you, I think , do not.  What I know reassures me.  It also causes me to
tremble with dread of the future.

   In the days to come, there will be recrimination and accusation,
fingers pointing to determine whose failure allowed this to happen and
what can be done to prevent it from happening again.  There will be
heightened security, misguided talk of revoking basic freedoms.  We'll
go forward from this moment sobered, chastened, sad, but determined
too.  Unimaginably determined.

THE STEEL IN US

   You see, the steel in us is not always readily apparent.  That aspect
of our character is seldom understood by people who don't know us well.
On this day, the family's bickering is put on hold.

   So I ask again:  What was it you hoped to teach us?  It occurs
to me that maybe you just wanted us to know the depths of your hatred.
If that's the case, consider the message received.  And take this message in
exchange:

You don't know my people.  You don't know what we're capable of.  You
don't know what you just started.

But you're about to learn....
```

Noone can condone what has happened.

But these problems will not be solved by demonising the other side. If you are
to understand the problem and solve it, you need to understand why there are so
many people willing to die in order to extract revenge on America. Why America
is despised in many parts of the world.

Look at the USA from the point of view of many of the ordinary people of the
Middle East. The USA

- maintains in power corrupt and undemocratic regimes so it can continue to
access cheap oil (eg Saudi, Kuwait)
- supports Israel in its continued exclusion of Palestinian people from their
ancestral lands
- has a track record of killing large numbers of innocent civilians when it
suited its interests (Hiroshima, Nagasaki, Dresden)

If you try and look at things from the point of view of a Palestinian refugee
who has no job, no hope and no great and powerful friends you may begin to
understand how these things happen.

To repeat, the murder of innocent civilians is not a legitimate thing to do, by
anyone.

Tim Josling

faults.

monsters, how are you going to understand what is happening? Remember,
they think you are evil monsters and look where it got them!

are simply evil megalomaniacs. But much of the breeding grounds for
terrorism come from poverty, hopelessness and betrayal of people's hopes.

Tim Josling

Or, if you prefer, 'ethnic'. There are people born within the boundaries of
Israel who cannot vote. On the other hand there are people not born within
Israel who can vote. The distinction is based on the racial/ethnic origin of

All I was trying to say here is that those who do not learn from history
will learn from their own mistakes.

After WWI, the victorious allies imposed ruinous reparations on Germany. The
result was a bitter, improverished electorate which in desperation allowed
Adolf Hitler to sieze power. In the resulting war, tens of millions of
people died.

After WWII, the victorious allies took steps to return both Germany and
Japan to stability and prosperity. A much wiser decision IMHO.

As long as there are millions of improverished and desperate people who
blame America for their problems, America will not be safe.

Tim Josling

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Terrorist Attacks (Very OT , but it needs to be said...)

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>

I don't normally air my politics and particularly not in a NewsGroup that is
supposed to be about COBOL.

However, your post ,Tim, has incensed me to the point where I must respond.

"Tim Josling" <tej@melbpc.org.au> wrote in message
news:3B9FC2B2.BC32F8B1@melbpc.org.au...
> Noone can condone what has happened.
>
No, That's right.

> But these problems will not be solved by demonising the other side. If you
are
> to understand the problem and solve it, you need to understand why there
are so
> many people willing to die in order to extract revenge on America.

First off, this is NOT the time to be making such observations. At the very
least you are demonstrating EXTREME bad taste, and there is no evidence that
"understanding" the problem will resolve it. Some political problems are
incapable of comprehension. The Irish are bombing the U.K in "payment" for
what Cromwell did 350 years ago... (at least that is what some would have us
believe; the fact that the IRA is a HUGE economic enterprise that robs Banks
and commits thuggery under the umbrella of "political" action seems a more
likely motivator for the continuance of their campaign, in my opinion.)

Secondly, these observations are based entirely on your own obvious
anti-American prejudice. Yes, it is a fact that there may be parts of the
World where America is not liked, but the reasons for this are not
necessarily the ones you propose. What about sheer envy? What about
resentment over the "Good Life" that Americans are supposed to enjoy? What
about a fundamental disagreement with the principles America stands for,
maybe based on Religious and Economic fanaticism? Do you think that people
in control of a repressive regime, based on fear and intolerance, are going
to be friendly to ANY State that tells them they are wrong?

Besides it doesn't matter whether you are right or I am, this tragedy goes
far beyond States and Politics. It strikes at the very base of Man's
inhumanity to Man.

Anyone capable of such an act does not need to be "demonised". Their actions
say it all... There is not now, and can NEVER be, political justification
for such an unthinkable action against people whose only crime was to be
born in a State that the perpetrators despise and abhor.

I don't care WHY they despise and abhor it...any sympathy I may have had for
their case evaporated when I saw people jumping to their deaths from the
WTC.


> Why America
> is despised in many parts of the world.
>
> Look at the USA from the point of view of many of the ordinary people of
the
> Middle East. The USA
>
> - maintains in power corrupt and undemocratic regimes so it can continue
to
> access cheap oil (eg Saudi, Kuwait)

Have you ever been to Saudi Arabia or Kuwait? I have. What evidence do have
that these regimes are "corrupt"? Billions of dollars of oil revenues in
Kuwait have been channelled back to the "ordinary people". Schools,
hospitals, Social Welfare programs have all been implemented in both Saudi
and Kuwait. Yes, these "regimes" are "undemocratic" but they are benevolent
"dictatorships" and they are based on the traditions of the people
concerned. The test is in talking to average citizens (I have done this...)
For the most part, the citizens of Kuwait and Saudi Arabia support their
rulers, and they don't do so out of fear or repression.

It is very easy to dismiss them as puppet states propped up by the US in
order to guarantee cheap oil. Believe what you want. If you are genuinely
interested, go there, observe and listen. Many people believed that Russian
Communism was the ideal system (before it collapsed in 1990). After going
there in 1987, I was VERY persuaded that, while Capitalism may be far from
perfect, it is WAY better than a regime founded on fear and repression.
Seems the majority of the Russian people agreed.


> - supports Israel in its continued exclusion of Palestinian people from
their
> ancestral lands
I have a great deal of sympathy for the Palestinian cause. I also have many
friends who are Jewish and some of them are Zionists. There is a VERY
convoluted history over who REALLY has the right to this land and we are
certainly not going to solve it here. It staggers me that you make
dismissive, sweeping statements about "ancestral lands" as if this can
justify the attacks on New York and Washington.

It would be fair to say the US has only ever brokered PEACE in this area.
Time and again successive US presidents have gone there to try and pour oil
on troubled waters and broker some kind of just resolution to the conflict.

How does this justify the action taken on Tuesday?

> - has a track record of killing large numbers of innocent civilians when
it
> suited its interests (Hiroshima, Nagasaki, Dresden)
>

You just get worse and worse... The raids on Dresden were ordered by  Bomber
Harris (check your history; he was BRITISH)... Hiroshima and Nagasaki were
acts of war, carried out in wartime, and warning was given to the Japanese
that a new technology was available to the Allies.

No Humanitarian can justify the the use of Nuclear weapons, and I am sorry
for what happened in these Japanese cities. But if it is a choice between
200,000 people dying  in a nuclear strike, or 2,000,000 dying in trying to
make a land invasion of Japan...well, the math is not hard to do.

> If you try and look at things from the point of view of a Palestinian
refugee
> who has no job, no hope and no great and powerful friends you may begin to
> understand how these things happen.
>
 I have people in my own town right here in New Zealand who have no hope, no
job, and no great and powerful friends. It does not induce them to hijack
civil aircraft and crash them into buildings.

Understanding is one thing; justification is quite another.


> To repeat, the murder of innocent civilians is not a legitimate thing to
do, by
> anyone.
>
Hold that thought. It 's the only one you got right.

Pete.

mean we hated Germans, and most certainly don't now. I spent two delightful
years in Germany and like the people greatly.

under the circumstances justified, using the logistics Pete gives below. I had a
dear friend, then a young R.N. officer who switched to the Marines. His job when
'Operation Invade Japan' happened - he would be landed surreptitiously on a
Japanese beach and hide for TWENTY-FOUR hours. Assuming he didn't get caught
first, he was then to act as a beach master directing the guys who were landing.
A more decent human being you couldn't meet. He had no regrets about either
Hiroshima or Nagasaki.

I mentioned VE and VJ days. There was no Boer War jingoistic jubilation that we
had beaten the 'Hun' or the little 'Nips'. As a kid I saw adults draw a HUGE
SIGH OF RELIEF. (Get a copy of Life magazine and you'll see the same happening
in Times Square). Thank God it was over. We have just finished the war to end
all wars (echoes of W.W.I). Regrettably that hasn't happened; I believe it was a
German commentator who noted that we have had some sort of war ever since, right
up to date..

struggle, you trying to tell me they thought Hiroshima and Nagasaki 'Just

a saying akin to "Faith, Hope and Charity. And the greatest of these is
Charity".

### Abend with Data Exception

- **From:** sergio_lima_costa@hotmail.com (Sergio Lima Costa)
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T06:22:36-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<deaf2c2f.0109120522.1817a5c4@posting.google.com>`

```
Hello.

Here we have a COBOL CICS PROGRAM that abend in OS/390 environment
with code 0C7 (Data exception)

Bellow the problem :



Hello. 

The offset 28B4 are in instruction of line 1839. 
After subtract X'28' from 28B4, I have 288C like result that are the
line 1831 of Cobol, Source.
Here after compile the program I have in my hand like bellow : 

Cobol Source : 

001831             IF      WC-IND                EQUAL   +0   OR 
001832                     WC-IND              GREATER   WC-QTD-LIN 
0018331                     MOVE    'ERRO. NAO POSICIONADO
CORRETAMENTE
0018341                                              TO  
L030-MENSAGEM
0018351                     MOVE    -1               TO   L030-CURSORL
0018361                     GO                       TO  
910-00-SEND-D
001837              END-IF 

001839              IF  WK-TRNID  EQUAL  'UN' 
0018401                 MOVE    'UNJ4'       TO   WTRANS 
001841              ELSE 
0018421                 MOVE    'OC04'       TO   WTRANS. 

Here Assembler Source : 

001831  IF 
   00287C  F910 204F C029          CP   79(2,2),41(1,12) 
   002882  4780 BC86               BC   8,3206(0,11) 
   002886  F911 204F 2051          CP   79(2,2),81(2,2) 
   00288C  47D0 BCA4               BC   13,3236(0,11) 
   002890                 GN=136   EQU  * 
001833  MOVE 
   002890  D222 63DA A230          MVC  986(35,6),560(10) 
   002896  9240 63FD               MVI  1021(6),X'40' 
   00289A  D229 63FE 63FD          MVC  1022(42,6),1021(6) 
001835  MOVE 
   0028A0  D201 2E47 AA73          MVC  3655(2,2),2675(10) 
001836  GO 
   0028A6  58B0 C03C               L    11,60(0,12) 
   0028AA  47F0 B000               BC   15,0(0,11) 
   0028AE                 GN=135   EQU  * 
001839  IF 
   0028AE  D501 2DE8 A509          CLC  3560(2,2),1289(10) 
   0028B4  4770 BCBC               BC   7,3260(0,11) 

After look this, Are sure that the problem are in instruction of line
1831 and not 1839, like I think before ?

Thank's 

Sergio
```

#### ↳ Re: Abend with Data Exception

- **From:** robert@jones0086.freeserve.co.uk (Robert Jones)
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T11:46:09-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fcd09c56.0109121046.4bc9f2be@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<deaf2c2f.0109120522.1817a5c4@posting.google.com>`

```
I would agree with you.  The IF statement is the only one shown that
could originate an OC4, it has two CP (compare packed) instructions
corresponding to the conditions in the IF statement.

However, another time it would be more helpful if you also included
the data definitions with the example.

Regards Robert

## Thread: Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe — 14 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe) · [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe

- **From:** Colin Campbell <cmcampb@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T11:26:04-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>`

```
Old IBM Mainframe COBOL programs that wanted the true record length of a
Variable Length record would play games with a subscript, reducing it to
-4, so that they could access the record descriptor word (RDW).

With new features of the 1985 ANSI COBOL standard, and IBM language
extensions in COBOL for OS/390 & VM, is it possible to get the actual
record size?  Should I keep playing the "trick" to get true record
length?

My program's FD has records described as "very short" (about 40 bytes),
and "very long" (about 1639 bytes), so the program knows that the file
contains variable length records.  There are 40+ record types coming in,
all in this range.  Right now, the program is acting as if one of
"intermediate length" record types is "very long", so it is wasting time
moving bytes that it doesn't have to.  I used LENGTH OF to acquire a
length, but this is just the described length of the "very long" record,
not the actual size.

The records do not have a "number of occurs" that would allow me to
compute actual sizes for different record types.  Because I am new to
the input data & program, I do not know whether a given record type
always has the same record length, although I suspect it does.
Thanks,
Colin
```

>

I just so happen to need to get a variable length with a project I'm working
on. What's this "trick" you mentioned?
```

##### ↳ ↳ The "Trick"

- **From:** Colin Campbell <cmcampb@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T14:16:00-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3B9FD08F.86B91FB9@ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net> <IjPn7.937$uc1.204771451@newssvr12.news.prodigy.com>`

```
Generally, the FD contains one record description of the form:
01  V-TYPE-REC.
  05 V-CHAR PIC X OCCURS 1 TO 1639 DEPENDING NO-OF-BYTES INDEXED V-X.
The Working-Storage contains:
01  NO-OF-BYTES BINARY PIC S9(4) VALUE +1639.
01  REC-LENGTH BINARY PIC S9(4).
01  REC-X        REDEFINES
    REC-LENGTH.
 05 REC-LENGTH-1 PIC X.
 05 REC-LENGTH-2 PIC X.
The Procedure Division has a READ, followed by some code like:
SET V-X     TO  1
SET V-X     DOWN BY  4
MOVE V-CHAR (V-X)  TO  REC-LENGTH-1
MOVE V-CHAR (V-X + 1)  TO  REC-LENGTH-2
Executing this code allows you to pick up the 16 bits in the RDW that contain
the actual record length (including the RDW itself, which COBOL adjusts for when
managing the records).  For this example, if I had a maximum length record,
REC-LENGTH would have a value of +1643, meaning that there were 1639 data bytes
in the record.

I believe that with 1985 COBOL, you could use reference modification, and code
MOVE START-REC-1(VAR-POS:2) TO REC-X
but that isn't what is in most old programs.

Once you have this actual length, you probably will want to subtract 4 from it.
Colin
```

#### ↳ Re: Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T16:11:59-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9noj72$3u8$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>`

```
Unlike pre-85 Standard COBOL's, there is a fully SUPPORTED and documented
way of getting the "actual" length of any variable length record that is
read in any CONFORMING '85 Standard compiler.

If in your FD you use the

  RECORD VARYING IN SIZE FROM m TO N
     DEPENDING ON WS-ITEM

where WS-ITEM is an unsigned integer data item defined in your
working-storage section.

PLEASE NOTE WELL: this is RECORD VARYING IN SIZE and it *replaces* the older
RECORD CONTAINS clause.

If you use this format, the WS-ITEM will include the record size of each
record - after it is read.  This technique is also useful in doing WRITEs -
but in that case, you put the value into the WS-ITEM before you do the
WRITE.

See:
 http://publib.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/IGYLR205/5.2.5.3

for complete details

Note: This method (unlike the subscript by -4) works even if files are above
the line and the FD doesn't point to the "real" buffer.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe

- **From:** Colin Campbell <cmcampb@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T14:19:23-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3B9FD15B.C993E4C2@ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net> <9noj72$3u8$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Bill,
As often before, you've come up with the solution that I'd read about, but not
used, and therefore forgotten!  It also points out that I didn't RTFM enough --
sorry for that!
Thanks,
Colin
```

#### ↳ Re: Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe

- **From:** sff5ky@aol.comxxx123 (Sff5ky)
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T22:05:51+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20010912180551.10163.00000012@nso-bg.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>`

```
In article <3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>, Colin Campbell <cmcampb@ibm.net>
writes:

>
>My program's FD has records described as "very short" (about 40 bytes),
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>

If you use the format of
    RECORD VARYING IN SIZE FROM x TO y 
          DEPENDING ON WS-RECD-LEN 
in the FD , then each read will be filled with the Actual record length.
You might be able to do some edits on the read process to compare/report
the RecordType/RecordLength of all records processed.

Build a table to identify RecordType/RecordLength/Count
for each variation of RecordType/RecordLength encountered.

Do you have any system utilities that might be able to produce 
an occurrence analysis of your file?
This might help isolate what record type is causing the overlength
 processing.
```

#### ↳ Re: Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe

- **From:** "WOB" <wobconsult@sprynet.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T18:07:00-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9nolv3$99j$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>`

```
In your FD specify :

RECORD IS VARYING IN SIZE FROM 40 TO 1639 CHARACTERS DEPENDING ON
WS-RECORD-LGTH.

In WORKING-STORAGE specify :

03  WS-RECORD-LGTH PIC  9(09) BINARY VALUE ZERO.

After the completion of the "READ" the field (data-name) WS-RECORD-LGTH will
contain the length of the record just read. By specifying a fullword, you
won't run the risk of high-order truncation, due to the TRUNC compiler
option. But, then again, you could specify PACKED-DECIMAL or DISPLAY, which
is your own preference, but is much less efficient than BINARY. Just make
sure that your picture clause can hold (at a minimum) 5-digits. With BINARY,
whether it's PIC 9(05) through PIC 9(09), it still occupies 4 bytes. This is
why (IMHO) it's pointless to define anything other than a 9(09) definition
for BINARY (4 bytes).

If you're going to "WRITE" a record, populate the field with the desired
record length value prior to the actual write.

Regardless of the data-type of the DEPENDING ON data-name integer, it must
be defined as unsigned.

This facility was introduced with COBOL2 and has carried forward into later
releases of COBOL.

HTH....

Bill

"Colin Campbell" <cmcampb@ibm.net> wrote in message
news:3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net...
> Old IBM Mainframe COBOL programs that wanted the true record length of a
> Variable Length record would play games with a subscript, reducing it to
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Problem Solved -- Thanks

- **From:** Colin Campbell <cmcampb@ibm.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T15:15:16-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3B9FDE74.897D0A2B@ibm.net>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>`

```
Thanks to those who pointed me at the RECORD VARYING ... clause.

My program is now handling the records at their actual length instead of the
maximum.  I know I read about this in the past, but I had forgotten about it
because of non-use.
Colin
```

#### ↳ Re: Getting true length of a variable length record - IBM Mainframe

- **From:** "DBuck" <dbuck@prairieinet.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T19:44:07-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9novdb$92o9e$2@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`
- **References:** `<3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net>`

```

Colin Campbell <cmcampb@ibm.net> wrote in message
news:3B9FA8BC.6CF2CB17@ibm.net...
> Old IBM Mainframe COBOL programs that wanted the true record length of a
> Variable Length record would play games with a subscript, reducing it to
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>

This is supported by specifying that:

RECORD IS VARYING IN SIZE
FROM min TO MAX DEPENDING ON
ws-variable

where "min" is the minimum record length, "max" is the maximum record
length,
and "ws-variable" is a working storage field (numeric) that you would like
the
actual length of the record returned into.  This field will be fulfilled
with each
read.
```

## Thread: IBM modifies "statement of direction" on SOMObjects and OO COBOL — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Object-oriented COBOL`](topics.md#oo)_

### IBM modifies "statement of direction" on SOMObjects and OO COBOL

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-12T17:23:09-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9nonak$2k$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
From this week's IBM announcement viewable at:
 http://www.ibmlink.ibm.com/usalets&parms=H_201-248

"There continues to be recognizable value in the ability to build COBOL
Object-Oriented (OO) applications that can be deployed on the S/390
platform, and the COBOL OO technology is currently based upon SO. For that
reason, IBM will continue to support SOM�-based COBOL OO applications on
OS/390 V2 and z/OS V1R1.

The Statement of Direction for SOMobjects as announced in Software
Announcement 200-352 , dated October 3, 2000, included plans to incorporate
the SOMobjects ADE as a part of the IBM COBOL for OS/390 and VM compiler
product, and move a subset of the SOMobjects RTL to the Language Environment
component of z/OS. Since this effort would not benefit our customers, while
improved interoperability of COBOL with Java and with the WebSphere
Application Server would, IBM will focus future enhancements to COBOL in
this direction.

It is strongly recommended that customers with programs which depend on
SOMobjects evaluate the WebSphere Family of products for replacement
purposes. There is no detailed migration strategy from SOMobjects due to the
many changes which have come about in the underlying technology.

For further information about WebSphere, visit:
    http://www.ibm.com/software/webservers/appserv/

For further information about IBM COBOL for OS/390 and VM, visit:
    http://www.ibm.com/software/ad/cobol/
"
```

## Thread: Simple arithmetic (?) — 13 msgs

### Simple arithmetic (?)

- **From:** hwinship@mindspring.com (HD)
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T07:48:05-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com>`

```
Greetings all,

I've been perusing the groups' postings here looking for some clues on
this, but I am unable to assimilate from the different examples
something that speaks more directly to my issue.  Any help would be
greatly appreciated.  Clearly, I'm not a COBOL programmer.

All I want to do is basic arithmetic on two fields.  I've tried to
define these as numeric with the implied decimal place.  All I'm
saying is that subtraction should be easy with like data types (coming
from a more strongly typed language) so what gives?

Here are the two fields from the copybook:
              10  POL-TPREM           PIC 9(9).
              10  POL-EPREM           PIC 9(9).

What I'm trying to do is to allow decimal places to be persisted in
those fields.  They will also be displayed on the screen as such.  I'd
like to derive a third field, UPREM (unearned premium) from the
difference of these two.  I've defined the WS-UEP as:

       01  WS-UEP   PIC 9(9).

The display in/out fields are defined as follows:
       01  DISP-PREM          PIC ZZZZZZZZZ.
       01  DISP-PREM-R REDEFINES DISP-PREM.
           05 DISP-PREM-OUT   PIC X(9).

I've messed around with the 9999999v99 definition but it doesn't seem
to get me anywhere in terms of not ABENDING when I try to execute the
compute.

In Summary, what I'd like to do is to be able to display and persist
monetary amounts in the TPREM and EPREM fields, then, on display, I'd
like to take the difference between the two and display that third
field as well.

Any help would be greatly appreciated.

Thanks,
HD
```

#### ↳ Re: Simple arithmetic (?)

- **From:** "Howard Brazee" <howard.brazee@cusys.edu>
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T15:49:04+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Qz4o7.470226$ai2.35256820@bin2.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com>`

```

On 13-Sep-2001, hwinship@mindspring.com (HD) wrote:

> All I want to do is basic arithmetic on two fields.  I've tried to
> define these as numeric with the implied decimal place.  All I'm
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
>            05 DISP-PREM-OUT   PIC X(9).


Numbers in CoBOL are strongly typed - but CoBOL does treat I/O somewhat
differently than is common in other languages:

A field described with a PIC ZZZZZZZ or 999.99 is not really a number -
numbers are moved here to be displayed - but the this field is not directly
usable as a number.   Think of it as directions to map the number onto a
printer.

So we have numbers that we do arithmetic with.   These may look like
9(9)V99.   The "V" is an implied decimal point that the compiler is aware
of, but isn't really in working storage.   Do whatever arithmetic you want
with this number, and then move that number to the display field (the
computer will map the number onto the correct format).

I don't see from your post how you are doing input.  But to figure out the
code, do the following:

Move 5 to WS-UEP.
ADD 2 to WS-UEP.
Move WS-UEP to DISP-PREM.
Display DISP-PREM.

(I don't know the command you will se for your display).   You should see  "
        7".

I currently don't use screen input with CoBOL, but after you have tried
this, you may wish to ask for help with your input.  Please state your
environment and compiler.  Someone who is more familiar than I am with your
compiler will surely assist.
```

#### ↳ Re: Simple arithmetic (?)

- **From:** John H Sleight Jr <nospam@newsranger.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T16:31:56+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<0c5o7.7089$%u4.41653@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com>`

```
You can try this:

01  wrk-tprem             pic x(9).
01  num-tprem             redefines
wrk-tprem             pic s9(7)v99.
01  ned-tprem             pic -(6)9.99.

01  wrk-eprem             pic x(9).
01  num-eprem             redefines
wrk-eprem           pic s9(7)v99.
01  ned-eprem             pic -(6)9.99.

01  wrk-uprem             pic -(6)9.99.



move pol-tprem    to wrk-tprem 
move pol-eprem    to wrk-eprem 
compute ned-uprem  = num-tprem - num-eprem
move num-tprem    to ned-tprem
move num-eprem    to ned-eprem

display  �pol-tprem = � ned-tprem
display  �pol-eprem = � ned-eprem
display  �pol-uprem = � ned-uprem

Comments:

Since the pol- flds are in a copybook it�s difficult to redefine them without
moving them to work fields.
The num- redefines create the cents positions and develops a sign in the event
you have a negative value in either fld.

The ned- flds create the edited version of the fields for display. This displays
a period (.) before the cents positions and a minus sign (-) if negative #s are
displayed. Leading zeros are also suppressed. 

HTH, Jack.






In article <a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com>, HD says...
>
>Greetings all,
…[39 more quoted lines elided]…
>HD
```

Try defining

           10  POL-TPREM           PIC 9(7)V99.
              10  POL-EPREM           PIC 9(7)V99.
       01  WS-UEP   PIC 9(7)V99.

The display in/out fields are defined as follows:
       01  DISP-PREM          PIC ZZZZZZZZZ.

MOVE WS-UEP TO DISP-PREM.

If this abends, one of your input fields is not numeric.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Simple arithmetic (?)

- **From:** hwinship@mindspring.com (HD)
- **Date:** 2001-09-14T07:53:45-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a1ad4b82.0109140653.1a7f1de6@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com> <jvyyrzubevmbagrfvasbezngvpnpbz.gjmhuq0.pminews@news.wanadoo.es>`

```
Hi,

Thanks all for the ideas.  Unfortunately, this is still not working. 
My only idea is that possibly the variable types for the fields
involved with the compute change(?) during the EDIT-PREMIUM function
(see below).  All three of the fields I'm using for this calculation
are defined identically.  And then it's only subtraction.

Thanks so much for any further thoughts.
Heather

Also, my environment is such:
compiler IBMVisualAge 3.0
deployed to TXSeries CICS running on WinNT
testing through TN3270Plus

The debug environment is grotesque.  I'm writing out to a log file and
using the cicssdt read FILE for debugging.

I defined the copybook members as follows:

              10  POL-TPREM           PIC 9(7)V99.
              10  POL-EPREM           PIC 9(7)V99.

In Working Storage:
       01  WS-UEP PIC 9(7)V99.

       01  WS-ORIG-PREM   PIC X(9).
       01  WS-NEW-PREM    PIC X(9).
       01  WS-NEW-PREM-R REDEFINES WS-NEW-PREM.
           05 WS-NEW-PREM-N PIC 9(9).

       01  DISP-PREM          PIC ZZZZZZZZZ.
       01  DISP-PREM-R REDEFINES DISP-PREM.
           05 DISP-PREM-OUT   PIC X(10).

--------------------------------
     
      * Moving Data from the Screen to working storage

      * TOTAL PREMIUM
               MOVE TPREM2I             TO WS-ORIG-PREM 
               PERFORM EDIT-PREM 
               MOVE WS-NEW-PREM-N       TO POL-TPREM 
      * EARNED
               MOVE EPREM2I             TO WS-ORIG-PREM 
               PERFORM EDIT-PREM 
               MOVE WS-NEW-PREM-N       TO POL-EPREM 

----------------------
      * Formatting the display out
       EDIT-PREM.
            MOVE 10    TO SUB-ORIG.
            MOVE 9     TO SUB-NEW.
            MOVE ZEROS TO WS-NEW-PREM.
      
            PERFORM RIGHT-JUSTIFY-IT UNTIL SUB-NEW = 0 OR SUB-ORIG =
1.
      
       RIGHT-JUSTIFY-IT.
            SUBTRACT 1 FROM SUB-ORIG.
      
            IF WS-ORIG-PREM(SUB-ORIG:1) IS NUMERIC OR
                WS-ORIG-PREM(SUB-ORIG:1) = '.'
                
               MOVE WS-ORIG-PREM(SUB-ORIG:1) TO WS-NEW-PREM(SUB-NEW:1)
               
               SUBTRACT 1 FROM SUB-NEW
            END-IF.
                                 
       EDIT-PREM-EXIT.
            EXIT.

-------------------------------

      * Moving Data out to the Screen
      * TOTAL PREMIUM
              move POL-TPREM to DISP-PREM
              move DISP-PREM-OUT to TPREM2I
      
      * EARNED 
              MOVE POL-EPREM        TO DISP-PREM 
              MOVE DISP-PREM-OUT    TO EPREM2I 

      *>>>>>>>>>>>>>>> EXPLODES (ABENDS) HERE >>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
              compute WS-UEP = POL-TPREM - POL-EPREM

              move WS-UEP  to DISP-PREM
              move DISP-PREM-OUT to UPREM2I



"Willem Clements" <willem@horizontes-informatica.com> wrote in message news:<jvyyrzubevmbagrfvasbezngvpnpbz.gjmhuq0.pminews@news.wanadoo.es>...
> On 13 Sep 2001 07:48:05 -0700, HD wrote:
> 
…[63 more quoted lines elided]…

```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Simple arithmetic (?)

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-14T14:43:44-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9ntmo5$562$1@slb2.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com> <jvyyrzubevmbagrfvasbezngvpnpbz.gjmhuq0.pminews@news.wanadoo.es> <a1ad4b82.0109140653.1a7f1de6@posting.google.com>`

```
Skipping all the "recent" stuff, but beleiving your description of what you
want to do.
Although you never say it - I think that what you want is to allow your
"user" to enter numeric  fields that are LEFT justified on a screen but
contain decimal points - do subtraction and in an output field display the
results in another field - also with decimal points.  For the code at the
bottom of this note, I am assuming the following (let us know if these
assumptions are not correct)

1) You are using a "current" COBOL compiler that supports intrinsic
functions
2) It is OK if your output field is right justified on the screen - but with
leading zero suppression.  If you need your output field to be left
justified, this can be done too - but would take a couple more statements.
3) If your input field contains signs (+ or -) but not currency signs, then
you can use this same routine - but add another byte to the input field.  If
your input DOES include curency signs, then switch from NumVal to NumVAL-C
as the appropriate intrinsic function.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Simple arithmetic (?)

- **From:** John H Sleight Jr <nospam@newsranger.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-15T05:16:02+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<muBo7.560$p77.2616@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<a1ad4b82.0109130648.509f6691@posting.google.com> <jvyyrzubevmbagrfvasbezngvpnpbz.gjmhuq0.pminews@news.wanadoo.es> <a1ad4b82.0109140653.1a7f1de6@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi HD,

Now that we see the fields come from a CICS map, it opens the problem into othe
areas.

I don't think your error routine is robust enough to handle all variations of
the numeric fields you're accepting, e.g. a 999.9999 entry would result in a 
99999V99 used in the computation; not good. A 4o99.99 entry would result in a
499V99 used in the computation; ditto.

You could first remove the spaces (leave the period (.)), check for the period
in the proper position, then remove period, then do "if numeric" test. If either
test is unsuccessful, reject the field. Pseudo code follows:

Move each non-space byte to a work field defined or redefined as below:

01 wk-fld-1.
05 wk-dollars    pic x(007).
05 wk-assumed-dp pic x(001).
05 wk-cents      pic x(002).

if wk-assumed-dp not = '.'
perf error-rtn
exit etc.
end-if
move wk-fld-1 data to wk-fld-2 using "move corr" as defined below:

01 wk-fld-2.
05 wk-dollars    pic x(007).
05 wk-cents      pic x(002).
01 wk-fld-2-num     redefines
wk-fld-2              pic 9(007)V99.   

if wk-fld-2 is not numeric
perf error-rtn
exit etc.
end-if



In article <a1ad4b82.0109140653.1a7f1de6@posting.google.com>, HD says...
>
>Hi,
…[157 more quoted lines elided]…
>> http://www.brainbench.com
```

function)

```
I thought about this too, but the "byte by byte" approach that appears in
this thread ALSO did not do "data validation".  Therefore, it is true that
you need to check your input. In the draft COBOL Standard, there is a
function TEST-NumVal to do this - but that isn't available in VisualAge
COBOL (or any other COBOL that I know) yet.  Therefore, you should do "data
validation" on user input (as always) - and I agree with this.
```

#### ↳ Re: Simple arithmetic (?)

```
1. If the fields are monetary they should be defined as:


                 10  POL-TPREM           PIC 9(7)V9(2)..
                 10  POL-EPREM           PIC 9(7)V9(2).

I assume you want to:

COMPUTE UPREM = POL-TPREM  -  POL-EPREM

define
                 10  U-PREM           PIC 9(7)V9(2).


The dec pts will "line up" and the compute will work.

If the output field is:

>        01  DISP-PREM          PIC Z(6)9.9(2).

then move U-PREM to DISP-PREM   all should be OK.

TA

## Thread: How to open ESDS file? — 12 msgs

_Topics: [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files) · [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** "-= Joe =-" <cch@asiaonline.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-14T00:22:50+08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net>`

```
    I have declared the ESDS file as SEQUENTIAL in the COBOL Program.

    Treat it as a SAM file, read it sequentially.

    However, I cannot OPEN the ESDS file.

    e.g. OPEN INPUT/I-O/OUTPUT/EXTEND XXXXX-FILE
    How could I possiblly open an ESDS file?
```

#### ↳ Re: How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** John H Sleight Jr <nospam@newsranger.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T16:51:21+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<du5o7.7113$%u4.42081@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net>`

```
Hi Joe,

You don't tell us all the clauses in the select. It is a VSAM file, so you must
use ORGANIZATION IS SEQUENTIAL, ACCESS IS SEQUENTIAL, FILE-STATUS IS WS-etc.

If you've done this, OPEN shouldn't be a problem.

You use INPUT if the file already exists and you want to read its contents.
You use EXTEND if the file already exists and you want to add records to the end
of the file. Just remember that the must be in ascending key sequence and of a
key higher than the last record key in the existing file.
You use I-O to update any existing record "in place" by using the READ/REWRITE
sequence.
OUTPUT, of course, is used when creating a new file.

HTH, Jack.



In article <9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net>, -= Joe =- says...
>
>    I have declared the ESDS file as SEQUENTIAL in the COBOL Program.
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** stephenjspiro@hotmail.com (Stephen J Spiro)
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T15:36:40-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4145699b.0109131436.5740fb71@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net> <du5o7.7113$%u4.42081@www.newsranger.com>`

```
John H Sleight Jr <nospam@newsranger.com> wrote 

> Hi Joe,
> 
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> key higher than the last record key in the existing file.
<snip>

*-------------------
There are no keys on an ESDS file -- that's the whole point.  It's a
sequential file built and managed with Access Methods Services instead
of the IOCS.  And unlike BSAM/BDAM, you cannot redefine it to access
it another way.

Stephen J Spiro
President
Wizard Systems
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** John H Sleight Jr <nospam@newsranger.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-15T00:55:57+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<xGxo7.371$p77.2533@www.newsranger.com>`
- **References:** `<9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net> <du5o7.7113$%u4.42081@www.newsranger.com> <4145699b.0109131436.5740fb71@posting.google.com>`

```
The model I had in mind (but sadly didn't mention) when I referenced "keys", was
using an ESDS as a "flat" backup and potential load input for a KSDS.

The "keys" in question were "logical keys", not an index, and they must maintain
the identical sequence if the index in the original KSDS (BTW, ESDSs CAN have
alternate indexes in a CICS envornment).

I should have mentioned that this was a specialized use of an ESDS and that an
ESDS need not (but can) be created in any sort sequence.

#### ↳ Re: How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** Volker Bandke <vbandke@bsp-gmbh.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T20:50:40+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<2rv1qtg3t92vfrrudr8pnhq0km2k4cc91d@4ax.com>`

```
Dis you put the AS prefix to the file name on the SELECT statement:

 *                                    +---- this is important   
 *                                    !
        SELECT MY-ESDS-FILE ASSIGN TO AS-MYESDS
            ORGANIZATION IS SEQUENTIAL
            ACCESS MODE IS SEQUENTIAL
            FILE STATUS IS FILE-STAT VSAM-STAT.




        OPEN INPUT MY-ESDS-FILE

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-13T22:08:02-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9nrsd0$h26$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net> <zico7.888$l76.141336@dfiatx1-snr1.gtei.net> <9nrpe7$ddm3@imsp212.netvigator.com>`

```
As pointed out in another post, it is what is in your ASSIGN clause that is
causing the problem.

Change:

 SELECT BFEXCEPT-FILE ASSIGN       TO BFEXCEPT

    to

SELECT BFEXCEPT-FILE ASSIGN       TO AS-BFEXCEPT

This is documented in the current IBM LRM at:

 http://publib.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/igylr205/4.2.3.1
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: How to open ESDS file?

- **From:** Volker Bandke <vbandke@bsp-gmbh.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-14T09:11:31+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<0ab3qts7kudl8utk922l9i5ks62nnr21pi@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<9nqmaf$20ea$1@adenine.netfront.net> <zico7.888$l76.141336@dfiatx1-snr1.gtei.net>`

```
ORGANIZATION IS RELATIVE is used for VSAM RRDS
ORGANIZTION IS INDEXED for VSAM KSDS
ORGANIZATION IS SEQUENTIAL for VSAM ESDS

The AS- prefix in the SELCT is required to distinguish between QSAM
(using a DCB) and VSAM (using an ACB) sequential files

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Powercobol Ver 5.0 and ADO

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-09-15T13:04:03+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3ba2a9c0_4@news.newsgroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9nsp7h$1jm$1@usenet.otenet.gr> <3BA20EB4.79930EA@attglobal.net>`

```
I would like to know your basis for saying this, Carlos.

I have used DAO with Version 5, invoking it through *OLE, and I see no
reason why I couldn't do the same with ADO (although I haven't tried it).

Have you tried using ADO with Version 5 or has some salesman told you it can
only be done with V6.1?

In fact, there is very little you can do with version 6.1 that CAN'T be done
with version 5 (the Java interface is the only thing I can think of
immediately, and this is not so great in V6.1. It does not allow Java to
Call COBOL, only COBOL calling Java. As a consequence I am currently writing
my own Java interface for V5. )

Although I have bought and paid for V6.1 and have the CD available, I will
not install it for the following reasons:

1. It provides no major benefit over V5 (Unless you move to the Enterprise
Edition, and I'm not prepared to do that...)

2. The license does not support easy uninstall or re-install and, if you
live outside the United States, it is not viable to simply call Fujitsu when
you need to re-install. (Apart from the cost, there are time differences to
be considered. I have also found in the past, that, while phone support from
Fujitsu is very good, there are often problems in reaching them via their
mail server.)

3. The resources required to support V6.1 are more than I am currently
prepared to devote to it, especially when the "additional features" are nil.

The above reasons mean that I am unlikely to install V6.1 in the near
future. V5 meets my requirements adequately and will very likely be the last
product I install from Fujitsu. (I am reserving judgement on the .NET
compiler to see if the same insane licensing policy applies to it... If it
does, I will either move to another vendor or move away from COBOL
altogether.)

There is a tendency to believe that whatever is "latest" must be best.

In the case of Fujitsu COBOL Professional Edition, this is just NOT true.

Pete.

"Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message
news:3ba40a24_8@news.newsgroups.com...
[snip...]
> However, I re-iterate: It should be possible to invoke ANY OLE compliant
> software from Power COBOL V5, using the Fujitsu supplied *OLE Class.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
I'm not using V6 either for the same reasons you stated. However, I think
that V6, as an host environment, has the ability to provide "control
binding" (as in VB6). As a result, it is possible to bind a data control
(ADO) to a visual control (say a combo box) and automate the load of the
combo or even persist the input from screen.
On the other hand, we both know that the *OLE Class has it's own
limitations. For instance, it doesn't have any provisions to trap events
generated by the OLE server, which in some circumstances, is absolutely
needed. May be if we could reference the .tlb files, we could achieve early
binding and the PowerCobol pre-processor could provide a wrapper class to
handle the OLE Server events (as it is done in C++).

Paulo Vieira
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Powercobol Ver 5.0 and ADO

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2001-09-17T21:50:32+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3ba5caf3_3@news.newsgroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9nsp7h$1jm$1@usenet.otenet.gr> <3BA20EB4.79930EA@attglobal.net> <3ba2a9c0_4@news.newsgroups.com> <3BA33BC2.3B4F51D7@attglobal.net> <3ba40a24_8@news.newsgroups.com> <9o4c4i$jao$1@venus.telepac.pt>`

```
"Paulo Vieira" <pvieira@emporsoft.pt> wrote in message
news:9o4c4i$jao$1@venus.telepac.pt...
>
> "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> combo or even persist the input from screen.

Personally, I'm not keen on bound controls, preferring to get my data
manually. I tried the Fujitsu supplied database control and it worked fine
but I don't use it; I use ODBC and ESQL.

I have tried data bound grids as third party ActiveX controls with V 5.0 and
they certainly work fine. I still don't like it...just a personal
preference.

 > On the other hand, we both know that the *OLE Class has it's own
> limitations. For instance, it doesn't have any provisions to trap events
> generated by the OLE server, which in some circumstances, is absolutely
> needed.

Sorry, you may know that, but I certainly don't <G>. There is a specific
*OLE EXCEPTION Class which DOES trap errors at the OLE server and returns
full details of them to the invoker.

>May be if we could reference the .tlb files, we could achieve early
> binding and the PowerCobol pre-processor could provide a wrapper class to
> handle the OLE Server events (as it is done in C++).

OO COBOL (and PowerCOBOL) does this better than C++ (in my opinion), because
there is no need to deal with the details of .tlb, C type Header, or any of
the ActiveX wrapping... you just instantiate the Exception class and point
it at the OLE server you want exceptions notified from. (I would stress that
I only used it once to check it out; most of the time if I have a server
failure, I abort the transaction).

Obviously, it is "horses for courses", however I do a lot of tricky direct
RDB
analysis and maintenance using DAO and it works fine (even bypassing the
*OLE class and referencing the Database Objects and Methods directly), hence
I feel ADO should be no problem.

Pete.

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>

Ah, I see where you're coming from now...<G>

I'm not convinced it can't be done, PROVIDED the OLE Client makes its events
visible. ActiveX controls (which are really just OLE servers "wrapped" in a
standard way) can (and in some cases do) reveal their Methods, Properties,
and Events.

Have you checked the Excel documentation to see what Methods, Properties,
and Events are available to OLE? Maybe ADO itself supports certain event
detection?

I wouldn't personally be looking for a "Window Deactivate"... but I
understand what you're saying...

If you really are so desperate to look for this level of event (and there
may well be cases where you are) then why not invoke the Windows API and
check the message loop? (Talk to Windows directly rather than OLE).

Pete.

## Thread: Acessing "RETURN-CODE" register — 10 msgs

### Acessing "RETURN-CODE" register

- **From:** mshetty@mail.com (mshetty)
- **Date:** 2001-09-15T05:50:26-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bfbb8fd4.0109150450.375d8cc4@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi,

I am invoking a COBOL subprogram in my C prog. I am able to access the
value of "RETURN-CODE" if the COBOL prog terminates normally.

But if my COBOL prog throws a DIVDE BY ZERO error, the control does
not return to the calling C program.

Following is the error thrown by COBOL
**********************************************************************
KCCB0002R-S(1)
A divide exception occurred in a numeric item.
Program-name = CBL_QUERYBOOKNAME
Line number / column = 000012/09

**********************************************************************

Please let me know if there is a way to return control to the calling
C prog so, that appropriate action can be taken.

My COBOL sub-program ends with an -EXIT PROGRAM statement.

Thanks and Regards,
M Shetty
```

#### ↳ Re: Acessing "RETURN-CODE" register

- **From:** Volker Bandke <vbandke@bsp-gmbh.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-15T15:32:36+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3vl6qt4c9krfole3gf4culhpl82ltq0790@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<bfbb8fd4.0109150450.375d8cc4@posting.google.com>`

On 15 Sep 2001 05:50:26 -0700, mshetty@mail.com (mshetty) wrote:

>Hi,
>
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>M Shetty


In the sub-program:

IF DIVISOR =0 THEN
   MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
   GOBACK
ELSE
   COMPUTE My-result = Divident / Divisor
END-IF

#### ↳ Re: Acessing "RETURN-CODE" register

- **From:** Volker Bandke <vbandke@bsp-gmbh.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-15T15:36:44+02:00

```
Another option (in the sub-program)

COMPUTE My-result = Dividend / Divisor
   ON SIZE ERROR
      MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
      DISPLAY ' There was a division by zero
      GOBACK
END-COMPUTE

#### ↳ Re: Acessing "RETURN-CODE" register

```

mshetty <mshetty@mail.com> wrote in message
news:bfbb8fd4.0109150450.375d8cc4@posting.google.com...
> Hi,
>
…[21 more quoted lines elided]…
> M Shetty

You have to catch it before the ABEND.  You can do this several ways, but
the easiest is to either check your divisor (if statement) or use ON SIZE
ERROR on the DIVIDE/COMPUTE statement.  Either way, you will have to set a
return code for you calling program to find.

1)  IF divisor = ZERO
        MOVE number TO RETURN-CODE
        GOBACK
     END-IF.
     DIVIDE field-a BY divisor .....

2)  DIVIDE field-a BY divisor
         ON SIZE ERROR
              MOVE number TO RETURN-CODE
              GOBACK.
     ..........


Hope this helps,
Dave
```

One possible technique if you only have one good exit is to make that return
a specific non zero RETURN-CODE.  Then that value can be used to show a good
return and anything else (including zero) means there was an error.

Hi M,

I am not aware on which platform you are programming and what versions of C and
COBOL you are using. Please have a look in your current COBOL programming guide.
I'd guess that you are allowed to use the 'ON SIZE ERROR' phrase in your DIVIDE
statements:

Try the following little program on your system which obviously makes no sense,
but should run and give you a return-code of 111 instead of an abort:

IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.                     
PROGRAM-ID. DIVIDE-ERROR.                  
DATA DIVISION.                               
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.                    
01 DIVISOR  PIC S9(5) COMP-3 VALUE ZERO.   
01 DIVIDEND PIC S9(5) COMP-3 VALUE ZERO.   
01 RESULT   PIC S9(5) COMP-3 VALUE ZERO.   
PROCEDURE DIVISION.                          
MAIN SECTION.                                
DIVIDE DIVIDEND BY DIVISOR GIVING RESULT 
ON SIZE ERROR PERFORM S10-DIVIDE-ERROR  
NOT ON SIZE ERROR CONTINUE              
END-DIVIDE                               
GOBACK.                                  
S10-DIVIDE-ERROR SECTION.                    
MOVE 111 TO RETURN-CODE               
GOBACK.                                  
END PROGRAM DIVIDE-ERROR.                    

On 15 Sep 2001 05:50:26 -0700, in article
<bfbb8fd4.0109150450.375d8cc4@posting.google.com>, mshetty stated...

>Hi,
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…

#### ↳ Re: netexpress university edition and vb

- **From:** "Mike Kinasz" <mkinasz@cbspayroll.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-16T21:41:59+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<H09p7.16707$707.9027082@news2.rdc2.tx.home.com>`
- **References:** `<f73075b0.0109160446.7757d66d@posting.google.com>`

```
You can definitely mix VB and COBOL.... and in my opinion the way you
mention is the best method.  VB can dynamically invoke the DLLs you create
in COBOL.  Under "Project Build Settings, select the Link tab, under
Category select Advanced and put CBLRTSS.LIB under "Link with these OBJs:"

If you do not statically link them you will need the runtime files to be
present (CBLRTSS.DLL at least) or the DLL will not work.  I'm not familiar
with the university edition so i'm not sure if those files come with it or
not.......

Anyway since I doubt binaries are allowed here in the NG I'll email you a
zip file containing an .APP and a .CBL and a VB Project that shows data
going both ways.   If you never receive it, feel free to drop me an email...

Mike

<a id="t-3133070f86"></a>
## Thread: "not quite a contest" - Routine to validate "input" to NumVal — 6 msgs

### "not quite a contest" - Routine to validate "input" to NumVal

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-16T18:34:12-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9o3d1o$dia$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Given a recent thread (and not knowing WHEN any implementation will be
available for the draft COBOL Standard's Test-NumVal intrinsic function) - I
was wondering if this group would come up with some "standard conforming"
(85/89/93 - not 200x) routine for testing if a "passed parameter" would or
would not be valid input to the NumVal intrinsic function.  (Once this is
created, then we could work on NumVal-C).

"assumption(s)"
A) The subprogram compiles in a program with intrinsic functions - otherwise
there is no need for this routine.
B) Performance is not as important as "maintainability" - but performance is
certainly "nice to have"
C) I have used my "own" style in my start-up code below.  Feel free to
"modify" it as you think appropriate. (If you compile your program, make
certain that you compile it with ANSI Flagging on, so your routine is
*totally* ANSI/ISO conforming.)  Because of internet/Usenet "issues" - I
have *not* provided code beginning in column 7/8.  You may do this - or
indicate that it needs to be done.

"requirements"

1) Four Linkage Section fields:
   - an integer given the length of the string to be tested
   - a PIC X(1) field with the decimal point character (i.e. "," or ".")
  - an integer returning 0 if the field is valid and an integer (listed
below) if the input is invalid
  - the actual "alphanumeric" string to be tested  (assume USAGE DISPLAY)

2)  Rules for what is "valid"
  - There must be at least one digit (0-9) and no more than 18 digits
    return 1 if this rule is violated
  -  There may be leading and/or trailing spaces.
  - There may be NO spaces between the first non-space character and the
last non-space character - except as noted in the next two rules
    return 2 if this rule is violated
  - The first non-space character may be either "+" or "-" - if so there may
be spaces before the next non-space character - which must be a digit - and
the last non-space character must be a digit or the decimal-point (not a
sign character or string)
    return 3 if this rule is violated
 - The last non-space character (or two) may be "+" "-" "CR" "DB" (c, r, d,
b are  NOT case sensitive).  This may only occur if the first non-space
character is a digit or the decimal point character. If this/these are the
last non-space character(s) then there may be spaces preceding them before
the last digit or decimal point character.
    return 4 if this rule is violated
  - There may be 0 or 1 occurrence of the "decimal point" character (this
may be the first or last non-space character)
    return 5 if this rule is violated
  - All non-space characters must be digits or + or - or in the pair "CR" or
"DB" (case insensitive)
    return 6 if this rule is violated
  - If something else is "wrong"
    return 7

   ***

To start the program out (but I haven't tried compiling this yet <G>):

Identification Division.
 Program-ID.  Is-It-Valid-for-NumVal
Data Division.
 Working-Storage Section.
01    CheckForEnd    Pic X    Value "N".
        88  End-of-Loop            Value "Y".
 Linkage Section.
* Modify the following if you want to accept more than 999 byte input
01    LengPassed         Pic 9(3).
01    DecPointChar      Pic X.
        88  DPC-Comma        Value ",".
        88  DPC-Period          Value ".".
01    Return-Value        Pic 9.
        88  RV-OK                         Value 0.
        88  RV-not-1-18-digits         Value 1.
        88  RV-BadMiddleSpaces    Value 2.
        88  RV-Bad1stChar              Value 3.
        88  RV-BadLastChar            Value 4.
        88  RV-WrongNum-DP        Value 5.
        88  RV-BadInputChar           Value 6.
        88  RV-OtherError                Value 7.
01     Passed-String.
        05    EachByte  Occurs 1 to 999 times
                                depending on LengPassed
                                indexed by ByteInd
                                    Pic X.
Procedure Division Using    LengPassed
                                          DecPointChar
                                          Return-Value
                                          Passed-String.
Mainline.
    Perform HouseKeeping
    Perform LoopRoutine
        Until (Not RV-OK
             or  End-of-Loop)
    Perform WindUp
    Exit Program
     .
HouseKeeping.
    Set RV-OK to True
    Evaluate True
        When Not DPC-Comma and Not DPC-Period
            Set RV-OtherError to True
        When LengPassed Not Numeric
            Set RV-OtherError to True
        When LengPassed Zero
            Set RV-OtherError to True
        When Other
            Continue
    End-Evaluate
     .

LoopRoutine.
    Continue
    Set End-Of-Loop to True
     .
WindUp.
    Continue
     .
```

#### ↳ Re: "not quite a contest" - Routine to validate "input" to NumVal

- **From:** "JerryP" <news@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-18T21:31:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<G2Pp7.375450$NK1.35606121@bin3.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<9o3d1o$dia$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Well said:

Here's ours. Not nearly as robust as yours, but I needed something urgently
to deal with the obvious problem. In fact, I think I'll modify ours to
blank-fill the field on the first space after finding a digit. Then let the
calling program validate the magnitude of the result.

000182***************************************************************
000183*
000184*    J U S T V  - V A L I D A T E
000185*
000000*  RC(0)=OK, RC(1)=Invalid length, RC(2)=bad character found.
000186***************************************************************
000187 P300-DUMMY.
000188     ENTRY 'JUSTV' USING LINK-LENGTH LINK-DATA-GROUP.
000189     MOVE 0 TO RETURN-CODE.
000190     IF LINK-LENGTH < 2
000191         OR LINK-LENGTH > 18
000192         MOVE 1 TO RETURN-CODE
000193         GO TO P999-RETURN.
000194
000195     PERFORM VARYING IFROM FROM 1 BY 1 UNTIL IFROM > LINK-LENGTH
000196         EVALUATE LINK-DATA(IFROM)
000197             WHEN SPACE CONTINUE
000198             WHEN '0' THRU '9' CONTINUE
000199             WHEN '.' CONTINUE
000200             WHEN '+' CONTINUE
000201             WHEN '-' CONTINUE
000202             WHEN OTHER
000203                 MOVE 2 TO RETURN-CODE
000204                 EXIT PERFORM
000205             END-EVALUATE
000206         END-PERFORM
000207     GO TO P999-RETURN.

#### ↳ Re: "not quite a contest" - Routine to validate "input" to NumVal

- **From:** "DBuck" <dbuck@prairieinet.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-21T18:00:03-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9oggd4$boq39$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`
- **References:** `<9o3d1o$dia$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Here is another way to do it (not a better way, just a different way).  It
also supports numval-c (sort of, I couldn't remember off the top of my head
what special characters it allows):


CLASS POSSIBLE-NUMVAL IS '0123456789,.'
CLASS POSSIBLE-NUMVALC IS '0123456789,.$+-%'.

WORKING-STORAGE.

01 WORK-FIELDS                 COMP.
   05 S1                                    PIC S9(9) VALUE +1.
   05 S18                                  PIC S9(9) VALUE +18.
   05 ALL-SPACES                 PIC S9(9) VALUE ZERO.
   05 LEAD-SPACES              PIC S9(9) VALUE ZERO.
   05 END-SPACES                PIC S9(9) VALUE ZERO.
   05 ALL-PERIODS               PIC S9(9) VALUE ZERO.
   05 DOUBLE-COMMAS     PIC S9(9) VALUE ZERO.
   05 IMBED-SPACES            PIC S9(9) VALUE ZERO.

LINKAGE SECTION.
01 LINKAGE-PASSED.
     05 LINK-LENGTH            PIC S9(4) COMP.
     05 LINK-INFO.
          10 LINK-CHAR           OCCURS FROM 0 TO 999 TIMES
                                                DEPENDING ON LINK-LENGTH
                                                PIC X.

PROCEDURE DIVISION.

MOVE ZERO TO RETURN-CODE.

EVALUATE TRUE
    WHEN LINK-LENGTH = ZERO
    WHEN LINK-LENGTH > S18
         MOVE 16 TO RETURN-CODE
         GO TO 9999-RETURN
END-EVALUATE.

EVALUATE TRUE
    WHEN LINK-LENGTH = S1
       AND LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) NUMERIC
         GO TO 9999-RETURN
    WHEN LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) = SPACES
        MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
        GO TO 9999-RETURN
    WHEN LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) POSSIBLE-NUMVAL
        CONTINUE
     WHEN LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) POSSIBLE-NUMVALC
        MOVE 2 TO RETURN-CODE
     WHEN OTHER
        MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
        GO TO 9999-RETURN
END-EVALUATE.

MOVE ZERO TO ALL-SPACES, ALL-PERIODS, DOUBLE-COMMAS
                              LEAD-SPACES, END-SPACES, IMBED-SPACES.

INSPECT LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) TALLYING
       ALL-SPACES FOR ALL SPACES
       ALL-PERIODS FOR ALL '.'
       DOUBLE-COMMAS FOR ALL ',,'.

INSPECT LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) TALLYING
         LEAD-SPACES FOR LEADING SPACES.

INSPECT FUNCTION REVERSE (LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH)) TALLYING
         END-SPACES FOR LEADING SPACES.

COMPUTE IMBED-SPACES =
         ALL-SPACES - (LEAD-SPACES + END-SPACES)
END-COMPUTE.

EVALUATE TRUE
   WHEN ALL-PERIODS > S1
   WHEN DOUBLE-COMMAS > ZERO
   WHEN IMBED-SPACES > ZERO
       MOVE 8 TO RETURN-CODE
       GO TO 9999-RETURN
END-EVALUATE.

9999-RETURN.
GOBACK.

Enjoy....

Dave
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: "not quite a contest" - Routine to validate "input" to NumVal

- **From:** "DBuck" <dbuck@prairieinet.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-22T13:48:13-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9oim0t$d868a$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`
- **References:** `<9o3d1o$dia$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net> <9oggd4$boq39$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`

```

DBuck <dbuck@prairieinet.net> wrote in message
news:9oggd4$boq39$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de...
> Here is another way to do it (not a better way, just a different way).  It
> also supports numval-c (sort of, I couldn't remember off the top of my
head
> what special characters it allows):
>
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
>          GO TO 9999-RETURN

*** actually, this should be changed to not care if the length is 1, if the
entire field is numeric, it is good

should read:

WHEN LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) NUMERIC
      GO TO 9999-RETURN

>     WHEN LINK-INFO (1:LINK-LENGTH) = SPACES
>         MOVE 12 TO RETURN-CODE
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

<a id="t-a96456793d"></a>
## Thread: i-o file — 9 msgs

### i-o file

- **From:** "Luc Claerebout" <luc.claerebout@pandora.be>
- **Date:** 2001-09-17T15:37:41+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9Nop7.58564$6x5.12609244@afrodite.telenet-ops.be>`

```
I would like to add the ISBN numbers to a file where 350 titles of books are
stored. To write to a new file you have to use to open output file along
with the write record instruction. To read a file you have to use the open
input file along with the read file next record, but what about to add the
ISBN number to a already existing file. I know I must use the open i-o file,
but where can I write the ISBN number to and how.
```

#### ↳ Re: i-o file

- **From:** "James J. Gavan" <jjgavan@home.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-17T17:24:39+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BA63307.274C127B@home.com>`
- **References:** `<9Nop7.58564$6x5.12609244@afrodite.telenet-ops.be>`

```


Luc Claerebout wrote:

> I would like to add the ISBN numbers to a file where 350 titles of books are
> stored. To write to a new file you have to use to open output file along
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> but where can I write the ISBN number to and how.

I think what your are telling us is the following :-

    01 MyBookRecord.
        05 BookName            pic x(...)
        05 BookAuthor           pic x(...
        05 BookPublisher       pic x(...
        05 Book etc......

Now you've decided you want to add the ISBN. There really are only two
possibilities :-

(a) Does your BookFile have a filler in the record currently not used that could
fit
    the ISBN ?

    if yes - make a copy of your existing record, and taking above :-

    01 MyBookRecord.
        05 BookName            pic x(...)
        05 BookAuthor           pic x(...
        05 BookkPublisher      pic x(...
        05 Book etc......
        05 filler                        pic x(30).

You now take the filler field and split it for your new file record :-

        05 Book-ISBN           pic x(15).    *> the 'fifteen" is a guess
        05 filler                        pic x(15).

Note : we are NOT changing the size of the record.

As an ABSOLUTE minimum you  Open I/O using your new record format and INITIALIZE
the field Book-ISBN to spaces. Read Next record, Initialize Book-ISBN, REWRITE
record. Subsequently you can update the file with ISBNs when they become
available. (Possibly easiest way to do this would be to generate an
Ascii-Delimited/CSV that your users can edit manually to add ISBNs. Then you
take their finished list and re-input to create a new OUTPUT file containing the
ISBNs).

(b) If you haven't got a filler area - you are screwed. So still take a copy of
your original Book- record1 and create a copy file with Book-record2 which has
the additional field Book-ISBN. (Here we have INCREASED the size of the record).
Your conversion program - Open INPUT Book-record1 file, and use Read Next
record. Open as OUTPUT the file with Book-record2. On each Read Next move the
data from Book-record1 to Book-Record2 - ensure you initialize that Book-ISBN
field, now WRITE to file book-record2.

Having got your NEW file with Book-records2 you ignore the Book-Record1 file
altogether. Again suggest you create a CSV to get ISBNs into your new file.

Some may suggest slight changes to the above routines, but it will get you
there.

Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: i-o file

- **From:** "Warren Simmons" <warren.simmons@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-18T03:06:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gTyp7.29221$KV3.2429608@bgtnsc04-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<9Nop7.58564$6x5.12609244@afrodite.telenet-ops.be> <3BA63307.274C127B@home.com>`

```
The main point of this exchange is to know your requirements as much as you
can, and if you feel that something else will be needed for some unknown (or
known) reason, pad your record descriptions within reason.

Then when the need occurs, you may be home free.

Warren Simmons

#### ↳ Re: i-o file

- **From:** Steven Barney <sb47199@earthlink.net>
- **Date:** 2001-09-17T22:09:23+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3BA67485.A1AB4AB3@earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<9Nop7.58564$6x5.12609244@afrodite.telenet-ops.be>`

```
If you're working on an IBM mainframe, you can only open a file for I-O and
rewrite a record if the file is indexed (VSAM).  If it's a QSAM file, you'll
have to open the original file for input, read the record into working storage,
build your new record, and write the new record out to a new file.

I think the same would be true in MicroFocus CoBOL (but don't quote me.)

Hope this helps.

--Steve
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: i-o file

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-17T18:36:14-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9o61ia$97f$1@slb5.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<9Nop7.58564$6x5.12609244@afrodite.telenet-ops.be> <3BA67485.A1AB4AB3@earthlink.net>`

```
I cannot believe how common this MIS-conception is among IBM mainframe COBOL
programmers.  Ignoring for the moment ESDS files (which ARE "sequential"),
it is ENTIRELY possible to OPEN I-O QSAM files.  Obviously, those who think
this is not possible have not read the manuals and/or ever tried this.
(Instead they "think" about what should be logical).  It is REQUIRED that
any ANSI/ISO conforming implementation support OPEN I-O of ACCESS and
ORGANIZATION SEQUENTIAL files (if they support "direct access" type storage
devices).  And the IBM mainframe programmers are conforming in this respect.
If you "doubt" that this is well documented, see,

 http://publib.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/igypg205/1.8.2?

which says in part (and pretty clearly),

"You can also open QSAM files on direct access storage devices as I-O."
```

Hi Steve,

I think you have it wrong about Qsam files. As long as the file is disk resident
and the rewritten rec is the same size of the rec just read (the rewrite must be
preceeded by a read of the same rec), a REWRITE is permitted. See sect 6.2.31.5
Sequential Files of SC26-4769-04 COBOL Reference.

Regards, Jack.

## Thread: LE z/OS V1R2 - major change regarding COBPACKs (and SOMObjects) — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### LE z/OS V1R2 - major change regarding COBPACKs (and SOMObjects)

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2001-09-17T17:50:56-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9o5utu$7i3$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Although I doubt that many people are "up to" installing LE z/OS V1R2
immediately into production,  I did want to point out (and hope that you all
notice or pass on to your "responsible" systems *and* application
programmers) the following MAJOR (IMHO) change documented with this release
of LE.

According to:
  http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/CEEA6110/2.1.3

"The COBOL COBPACKs can no longer be modified. All of the COBOL COBPACK
modification jobs have been removed from SCEESAMP."

FYI - if you look at:
 http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/ceea5110/E.3?

You will see, however, that the "default" (only!!!) COBPACKs (IGZCPAC  and
IGZCPCO) are now RMODE(any) - which was the "usual" reason that COBPACKs
were modified (in the past).

P.S.  As I pointed out in another post,
 http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/CEEA6110/2.1.2

states,
"SOMobjects ADE and SOMobjects RTL have been removed from Language
Environment for z/OS V1R2."

P.P.S.  If you haven't seen it yet (although it has been available since
OS/390 V2R10), there is also some discussion of LE "downward compatibility"
functionality.

See:
 http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/ceea2110/1.2.2?
    and/or
 http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/ceea6110/2.3?
```
